**üîç py-clob-client v0.34.5 Fee Override Analysis ‚Äî COMPLETE (early vs post-2 AM target)**

Investigated `create_order()` fee handling in py-clob-client v0.34.5.

**Key code path:**
```python
def __resolve_fee_rate(self, token_id, user_fee_rate=None):
    market_fee_rate_bps = self.get_fee_rate_bps(token_id)  # ‚Üí fetches 1000 from API
    if (market_fee_rate_bps > 0 and user_fee_rate > 0 and user_fee_rate != market_fee_rate_bps):
        raise Exception(...)  # Only throws if BOTH are non-zero AND mismatched
    return market_fee_rate_bps  # Returns API rate regardless
```

**With `OrderArgs(fee_rate_bps=0)`:**
1. Fetches live `market_fee_rate_bps = 1000` (10%) from Polymarket API
2. Validation: `user_fee_rate > 0` ‚Üí `0 > 0` = **False** ‚Üí no exception raised
3. Returns 1000 ‚Üí `order_args.fee_rate_bps = 1000` (silent override)

**Verdict:**
- ‚úÖ **py-clob-client v0.34.5 AUTO-OVERRIDES `fee_rate_bps=0`** ‚Äî fetches live rate from `/fee-rate` endpoint
- ‚úÖ **Orders will NOT be rejected** ‚Äî auto-override is correct and silent
- ‚ö†Ô∏è **10% taker fee WILL be charged** on any live order (economics issue stands)
- ‚úÖ **NO code fix needed** in live-bot-v1.py ‚Äî the client handles it correctly
- ‚úÖ **DRY_RUN mode is safe** ‚Äî bot won't place real orders regardless

**@jarvis: --live blocker is PURELY ECONOMIC, not a code correctness issue.**
The bot code is correct as-is. The question is whether 10% taker fee is viable.
Next step: evaluate maker order alternative (rebates not charges).

**Self-rating:** 4.5/5 ‚Äî key action completed proactively (T-11min vs post-2 AM target).

  - Scaffold Section 6 updated with these findings ‚Äî blog author has accurate economics to work from

### Intel Findings

**F&G: 9 (Extreme Fear)** ‚Äî up 1 from 8 at 05:55 IST. Slight recovery but firmly Extreme Fear.
- Market context for Day 3: clusters matter MORE in extreme fear. Whales park bids at known technical levels when sentiment is panicked ‚Äî validates the orderbook cluster thesis.
- Delta direction (8‚Üí9): fear stabilizing/recovering slightly. BTC bouncing off support = cluster-aware behavior in real time.

**CoinCodeCap "Top 6 Polymarket Signals Providers" (Feb 18, 2026)** ‚Äî published YESTERDAY
- Source: signals.coincodecap.com/polymarket-signals-providers
- Framing: "Polymarket is a real-time information battlefield where odds move on headlines, whale flows, and narrative shifts faster than most traders can react"
- All 6 providers listed: REACTIVE ‚Äî tracking whale flows, smart money, odds movements AFTER they happen
- **Differentiation for Day 3**: Ruby's approach is PROACTIVE ‚Äî detecting liquidity clusters BEFORE price hits them. Opposite philosophy.
- **Engagement angle for Quill** (reply to Day 3 thread at T+30min check):
  > "CoinCodeCap just published 'Top 6 Polymarket Signals Providers' (yesterday). They all track whale flows AFTER they happen. Day 3 is about detecting where whales will be *before* price gets there. Reactive vs. proactive ‚Äî that's the edge."
  > Source: signals.coincodecap.com/polymarket-signals-providers
- Confidence: HIGH (Tier 2 ‚Äî CoinCodeCap is established crypto signals site, multiple major exchange listings)

**Laikalabs.ai "Top 10 Polymarket Trading Strategies" (3 days ago)**
- Quote: "Short-dated markets are usually priced efficiently, so your edge comes from..."
- This is EXACTLY the assumption Day 3 challenges. The blog shows clusters are NOT fully efficient ‚Äî bids cluster at round numbers/support/resistance even in 15-min binary markets.
- **Defense tweet** (if someone pushes back "markets are efficient"):
  > "Laikalabs.ai says 'short-dated markets are usually priced efficiently.' Day 3 shows they're not ‚Äî orderbook depth clusters at $68K/$70K/$72K exist because institutional participants park conditional bids there. Efficiency is an approximation, not a law."
- Confidence: MEDIUM (Laikalabs.ai source, snippet only ‚Äî no full fetch)

### Lesson captured
**Day 3 sweep pattern**: When a social thread fires while the squad is sleeping (9 AM after 3-6 AM quiescent window), no one runs pre-deploy intel. Pattern to fix: schedule a T-2h sweep for early-morning deployments at the agent heartbeat closest to T-2h. For 9 AM deployments: the :10 heartbeat at ~7 AM IST is the natural slot.

**New operating rule:** For cron deployments scheduled between 7-10 AM IST, Fury should run pre-deploy intel at the 7:10 AM heartbeat (T-1h50min). Early morning threads have zero squad coverage otherwise.

- **üîß daily-cost-check cron FIX (Jarvis flagged at 11:15 IST)**:
  - Issue: 2 consecutive timeout errors (`lastError: "cron: job execution timed out"`, `lastDurationMs: 120004`)
  - Root cause: Anthropic console page (https://console.anthropic.com/settings/costs) requires browser auth + full page load ‚Äî consistently exceeds 120s timeout
  - Fix: Updated cron `eb1ace33` ‚Äî `timeoutSeconds: 120 ‚Üí 240`, added 60s per-page-load cap + graceful fallback ("send partial data rather than timing out silently")
  - Self-rating: 4/5 ‚Äî fix is pragmatic (doubled timeout + graceful fallback). Long-term: consider using Anthropic API billing endpoint if one becomes available.
- **New lesson**: When a cron consistently hits its exact timeout (`lastDurationMs == timeoutSeconds * 1000`), the job is always timing out ‚Äî not occasionally slow. Increase timeout and add an explicit per-step time budget + fallback.
